<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-815723954374967367 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=815723954374967367><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=snidane8284 data-user-id=515302187031855114>snidane</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, February 28, 2021 8:15 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-815723954374967367>2/28/2021 8:15 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I don&#39;t think that how typed internal implementation of tensorflow is would matter to application programmers. They will keep calling high level dynamically typed functions. I do agree that performant library code will be written in low level languages with some static typing system. I don&#39;t agree that ober time we will see more static typing in application code for data processing. Go with generics would be useful for writing library code, competing with Rust, C++ or. Java. Neither of these are used for data processing.

Perhaps with the exception of Rust and Differential Dataflow which seems to be very promising model for pure stream processing with cycles and useful for algorithms for arbitrary graphs. Once it gets understood well enough I can imagine the embedded DSL to be extracted to a separate query language, but so far its query language is Rust based DSL.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

R = Row(&quot;id&quot;,&quot;age&quot;,&quot;serial&quot;)

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-819319145853091871 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=819319145853091871><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 10, 2021 6:21 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-819319145853091871>3/10/2021 6:21 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Questions i have asked ask if given a new source like that:

How is the file generated? Is it by an automatic process or semi-manual? What&#39;s the schedule? What&#39;s the nature of the data? Why does it contain PII, what is the PII used for? From a regulatory standpoint, how long do you need to/are allowed to keep the PII? Are the files full exports or delta files or a sliding window type export? 

All of that information informs you on how long you need to retain the original files in order to build a consistent picture at a point in time.

Then you get on to stuff like the schema, field formatting etc.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-821116952583602206 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=821116952583602206><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/97751494236848128/f8958b8da99b07774393c7c9e0fb3376.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=mashuma data-user-id=97751494236848128>jp</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 15, 2021 5:25 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-821116952583602206>3/15/2021 5:25 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title=".gcoder">@gcoder_done</span> If you are looking to process the content of a log file that is continuously being written to, then Filebeat can do that.

However, if you are looking for moving that file as it is created, then Filebeat is not an optimal option.

I did not read your original question and piggy backed off from someone mentioning Kibana.. 

Based on what you have wrote earlier
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">i have machines 10 machines(and more will come) each producing 1 file (5kb) per second. they are running continuously. I need to stream these files into a webserver where i have a script that grabs and uses them
</div></div>I think Filebeat + Logstash would be a good fit for you.

You&#39;d run Filebeat (very light weight, sort of agent daemon) on each node and stream the log file contents to Logstash server. Logstash then can process the stream or forward it into wherever you want.

Alternatively to Logstash, you can use elastic cluster, but without knowing what you expect to do with the log file content, it would be difficult to suggest to go with that. Elastic cluster may be an extreme overkill for what you are trying to achieve.

Have a look at these:
<ul><li>Filebeat input for Logstash <a href="https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/beats/filebeat/current/filebeat-input-filestream.html">https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/beats/filebeat/current/filebeat-input-filestream.html</a></li><li>Premade Logstash outputs <a href="https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/logstash/current/output-plugins.html">https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/logstash/current/output-plugins.html</a>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-821118486008561765 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=821118486008561765><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/97751494236848128/f8958b8da99b07774393c7c9e0fb3376.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=mashuma data-user-id=97751494236848128>jp</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 15, 2021 5:31 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-821118486008561765>3/15/2021 5:31 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Instead of &quot;moving&quot; these files, you would stream the file contents on some pre-configured rules.

Your pipeline may look like so..

[filebeat fleet] ===(data streams)==&gt; logstash (perhaps on your webserver?) ---&gt; some local file or files based on various filebeat provided metadata + some optional parsing with grok and other modules available for it.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-821118683371012096 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=821118683371012096><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, March 15, 2021 5:32 PM">5:32 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>If the connection drops, filebeat will &quot;queue&quot; and resume when it has re-established connection with .e.g logstash</span></div></div></div></div></div>

class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Irresistible APIs provides step-by-step guidance for designing APIs that reflect an application&#39;s core business value, delight the developers who use them, and will stand the test of time. In it, business product managers and developers learn how to treat an API as a first-class product.</div></div></div><div class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-container><a class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-link href=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/7g2k2XyYlGiYi67Arb4_b3cZEc9Cr0wX4lrU0-QPdpA/https/images.manning.com/360/480/resize/book/6/6a11f2f-9748-4e53-b714-c109345d85c5/Hunter_IAPIs_final.png> <img class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail src=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/7g2k2XyYlGiYi67Arb4_b3cZEc9Cr0wX4lrU0-QPdpA/https/images.manning.com/360/480/resize/book/6/6a11f2f-9748-4e53-b714-c109345d85c5/Hunter_IAPIs_final.png alt=Thumbnail loading=lazy> </a></div></div></div></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-822188509511024710 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=822188509511024710><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, March 18, 2021 4:23 PM">4:23 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Not big data specific but domain specific, probably a good place to start</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-823446732901187614 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=823446732901187614><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=tahir5710>tahir</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'823243545292177429')"> Hello there,

I have somehow managed to land a Data Engineer role. I have never been a Data Engineer before.
My background is DevOps (Linux for the last 15 years ,and also AWS, Ansible, systems, bash, python, networking, etc). 

At the interview they mentioned being in a Data Team and technologies and terms such as ETL, data pipelines, python, pytest, Jupiter Notebooks (with Pandas, numpy, matplotlib), AWS s3, data wrangling, Linux, SQL, Agile and doing code reviews in Github. I think I have either worked with some of these technologies and/or have played with some of them before but I don&#39;t know anything about ETL, data pipelines, pytest, Jupiter Notebooks (with Pandas, numpy, matplotlib),&#160; and doing code reviews to any great extent.&#160; Could someone point me to some recommend learning guides such as MOOCS, online courses etc about those (ETL, data pipelines, pytest, Jupiter Notebooks and doing code reviews)?

Also, what is it like to work in a Data Team, is it different to working in a Software Development Team? How best can I transition from a DevOps (mostly Linux sysadmin type experience) to a Data Engineer mindset? What would be some good things to figure out and ask questions about when you first start in a Data Team? 

Any help much appreciated. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=snidane8284 data-user-id=515302187031855114>snidane</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 22, 2021 3:43 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-823446732901187614>3/22/2021 3:43 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>As a Data Engineer you will write and/or maintain many little programs piping data around. Also you will be building a &quot;data platform&quot; ie. a coherent collection of tools which work together as seamlessly as possible. Mostly for &quot;big data&quot; processing and with requirements that it makes non-engineers happy. Everyone can process &quot;small data&quot; on their laptops, it&#39;s the big data that you will be help with and making the gap between small and big data processing as little as possible. It is not an easy task because of imperfect and still evolving tooling, but there is lot of value in helping the company extract value out of data, so it is understood that things will suck and you will help everyone overcome the barrier until perhaps a decade into the future when things could be more of self serve nature.

It&#39;s quite like devops but also isn&#39;t. You do write a lot python and bash. You deploy big data tools. You maintain data pipelines to keep them up and running. Since your are working on many little projects you will probably see a lot of trunk based dev, continuous integration instead of heavy release and packaging techniques.

With that - I&#39;ve seen devops people entering a data engineer role to be overly confident that it looks similar only to be too arrogant about their abilities.

The things mentioned above are not as important as understanding databases, data layout, sql, distributed data processing, history and evolution of big data tools.

Many things from traditional software dev don&#39;t apply. Testing is different, structuring code is different - eg. very little OO, databases typically used for webdev are useless.

Honestly in my experience the more experienced somebodu was in other software fields the more damaging their work became as they brought all the wrong concepts to it. Eg. Java people wrapping shit layers of classes for simple etl scripts because that&#39;s how they traditionally did things.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>3</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-823446808407310366 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=823446808407310366><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, March 22, 2021 3:43 AM">3:43 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It&#39;s better to start with a core team with experience in big data databases and then have them train juniors.

It is a new field with lot of traps. It&#39;s good to keep up with what&#39;s going on by watching conference talks - such as Data Council or Spark conf.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-823506152339800114 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=823506152339800114><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=snidane8284>snidane</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'823446732901187614')"> As a Data Engineer you will write and/or maintain many little programs piping data around. Also you will be building a &quot;data platform&quot; ie. a coherent collection of tools which work together as seamlessly as possible. Mostly for &quot;big data&quot; processing and with requirements that it makes non-engineers happy. Everyone can process &quot;small data&quot; on their laptops, it&#39;s the big data that you will be help with and making the gap between small and big data processing as little as possible. It is not an easy task because of imperfect and still evolving tooling, but there is lot of value in helping the company extract value out of data, so it is understood that things will suck and you will help everyone overcome the barrier until perhaps a decade into the future when things could be more of self serve nature.

It&#39;s quite like devops but also isn&#39;t. You do write a lot python and bash. You deploy big data tools. You maintain data pipelines to keep them up and running. Since your are working on many little projects you will probably see a lot of trunk based dev, continuous integration instead of heavy release and packaging techniques.

With that - I&#39;ve seen devops people entering a data engineer role to be overly confident that it looks similar only to be too arrogant about their abilities.

The things mentioned above are not as important as understanding databases, data layout, sql, distributed data processing, history and evolution of big data tools.

Many things from traditional software dev don&#39;t apply. Testing is different, structuring code is different - eg. very little OO, databases typically used for webdev are useless.

Honestly in my experience the more experienced somebodu was in other software fields the more damaging their work became as they brought all the wrong concepts to it. Eg. Java people wrapping shit layers of classes for simple etl scripts because that&#39;s how they traditionally did things. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title="Deleted User" data-user-id=456226577798135808>Deleted User</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 22, 2021 7:39 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-823506152339800114>3/22/2021 7:39 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I’m a fresh grad and noticed that most of the code for pipelines written by my seniors has very little OOP. 

Can you tell me a bit more about why?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-823565667302244362 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=823565667302244362><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title="Deleted User">Deleted User</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'823506152339800114')"> I’m a fresh grad and noticed that most of the code for pipelines written by my seniors has very little OOP. 

Can you tell me a bit more about why? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=snidane8284 data-user-id=515302187031855114>snidane</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 22, 2021 11:35 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-823565667302244362>3/22/2021 11:35 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>OOP was designed for simulations, for which there are better ways to code it these days using explicit time. It was popular for GUIs once, until Elm and React changed the paradigm. It also was meant to simplify game development, only for game devs to then realize that entity component systems are a better way to structure the code.

OOP really boils down to state management. In ETL code you want to do most of the processing stateless. If you actually need to preserve state between runs, then OOP doesn&#39;t help either, because OOP forgets state when program ends, unless you use some serialization trickery, but there better tools for that if you go down that way.

There&#39;s actually very little areas left for OOP. It is useful as a conceptual model, but doesn&#39;t translate well to machines.

Also: stop writing classes

We have a couple of tables from our source system that we need to pull to our DW. We&#39;re unable to query the underlying tables directly from prod so we pull from a replication server to our DW server before processing (politics, mainly).
The issue lies in that they are 1.5bn rows, and one in particular is 120 columns wide.
This is clearly a very, very large table.
I understand that taking only the columns we require will significantly reduce the size, but is there any benefit in other measures of optimising something this big? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=fnaxiom data-user-id=690875691293605899>Fnaxiom</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, March 23, 2021 7:52 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-824053020932571216>3/23/2021 7:52 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hmm. Have you considered the possibility of implementing  Change Tracking (either Change Data Capture or Change Tracking for SQL Server)? That can be used to get incremental changes and get updated/inserted/ deleted rows from source table. 
Basically, whenever you restore the replica, you query the changes that occurred since the last query</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-824053545858891836 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=824053545858891836><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, March 23, 2021 7:54 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-824053545858891836>3/23/2021 7:54 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We use solely SSIS and T-SQL.

The initial bulk is the issue, and maintenance mainly.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

id=chatlog__message-container-824060401738055780 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=824060401738055780><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Tuesday, March 23, 2021 8:21 PM">8:21 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>if you do go the clustered columnstore route, you should also do your best to align the stars such that table loads from SSIS go straight into compressed row groups:

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-826222932279820327 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=826222932279820327><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/672421268070596619/b9b254f8b83082ef575d0e034253f467.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=.deadvoid data-user-id=672421268070596619>deadvoid</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 29, 2021 7:34 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-826222932279820327>3/29/2021 7:34 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I mean admittedly a lot <em>can</em> be called logs, like for IoT data, they&#39;re practically event logs. They&#39;re useful for analysing bottlenecks &amp; to be part of some docs instead of tribe knowledge, but do those logs need to be treated as data or just artifact? Then when it comes to data from some APIs, there are vital business data &amp; there are types like remote connection failures, changes in API versions, etc., which are probably closer to metadata than core business data you expect to get. And so with all those kinds of logs, leads to stuffs like retention policy, auditing, filtering for GDPR, etc, I imagine those affect workflow or even pipeline aspects, like which storage to use, whether some logs need some processing at staging, or maybe some people just dump everything straight to data lake? Use separate tables that get cleaned periodically? It just seems like there are many ways to tackle logging scenarios, and there probably is some consensus on the best practices already</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-826225166576386110 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=826225166576386110><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/672421268070596619/b9b254f8b83082ef575d0e034253f467.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=.deadvoid>deadvoid</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'826222932279820327')"> I mean admittedly a lot <em>can</em> be called logs, like for IoT data, they&#39;re practically event logs. Successful DAGs pipeline logs, they may or may not be useful logs that needs to be stored, but how about failure logs? They&#39;re useful for analysing bottlenecks &amp; to be part of some docs instead of tribe knowledge, but do those logs need to be treated as data or just artifact? Then when it comes to data from some APIs, there are vital business data &amp; there are types like remote connection failures, changes in API versions, etc., which are probably closer to metadata than core business data you expect to get. And so with all those kinds of logs, leads to stuffs like retention policy, auditing, filtering for GDPR, etc, I imagine those affect workflow or even pipeline aspects, like which storage to use, whether some logs need some processing at staging, or maybe some people just dump everything straight to data lake? Use separate tables that get cleaned periodically? It just seems like there are many ways to tackle logging scenarios, and there probably is some consensus on the best practices already </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title="Deleted User" data-user-id=456226577798135808>Deleted User</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 29, 2021 7:43 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-826225166576386110>3/29/2021 7:43 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hello! In my company I developed an internal package that we use to lock scripts and automatic create logs.

The process is simple. If we want to run a specific script (lets say an API ETL). What we do is that first we create a Lock file and an empty log file (we define the paths) then we  can add INFO logs through the code blocks.

All code blocks are inside try-catch statements with an ERROR log. 

If a script fails, the catch statement will record the log and lock the script. Script locks do not allow the script to be run again until the error is fixed and the lock file is deleted.

Script logs are always kept in a directory and are used mostly for troubleshooting as they are recreated in every run.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-826225985757380628 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=826225985757380628><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/672421268070596619/b9b254f8b83082ef575d0e034253f467.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title="Deleted User">Deleted User</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'826225166576386110')"> Hello! In my company I developed an internal package that we use to lock scripts and automatic create logs.

The process is simple. If we want to run a specific script (lets say an API ETL). What we do is that first we create a Lock file and an empty log file (we define the paths) then we  can add INFO logs through the code blocks.

All code blocks are inside try-catch statements with an ERROR log. 

If a script fails, the catch statement will record the log and lock the script. Script locks do not allow the script to be run again until the error is fixed and the lock file is deleted.

Script logs are always kept in a directory and are used mostly for troubleshooting as they are recreated in every run. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=.deadvoid data-user-id=672421268070596619>deadvoid</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 29, 2021 7:47 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-826225985757380628>3/29/2021 7:47 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>So you overwrite the logs on each iteration of the script run?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

in general, the latter category of logs fall in store-all-the-things for me, because you need it when you need it, and you can&#39;t know when that is. these operational logs can be pruned pretty quickly, i think. retention of the former category of business-oriented-data-that-happens-to-be-log-like is again dictated by business needs.

in general, the latter category of logs fall in store-all-the-things for me, because you need it when you need it, and you can&#39;t know when that is. these operational logs can be pruned pretty quickly, i think. retention of the former category of business-oriented-data-that-happens-to-be-log-like is again dictated by business needs.

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-826866661163794504 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=826866661163794504><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/469151026751209483/1cb6bb474129683a69282980c1522d6f.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/331102813713203201/d7b2650199ce22862650cf8ca5d28495.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=gratisimo>monert151</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'826807565601603626')"> oh okay, in my case, I have a Pytorch model prediction endpoint (using AWS sagemaker), that I&#39;m creating in my driver. How would I be able to pass it to each of my executors (or partitions) so that each executor can call it (I&#39;m thinking of using mapPartitions, here). </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 31, 2021 10:21 AM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=toxicafunk data-user-id=469151026751209483>toxicafunk</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 31, 2021 2:12 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-826866661163794504>3/31/2021 2:12 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I don&#39;t know much about Pytorch or PySpark, but <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">mapPartitions</code> will probably do what u need</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-826867040140263475 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=826867040140263475><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 31, 2021 2:14 PM">2:14 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>1. u can pass the model to every executor so make sure its serializable
2. generate the model on each worker (if its not too time consuming)
3. have the model somewhere accessible by all workers (hdfs, s3, some url)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
